  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_0e67e2af-e3eb-41df-98b8-575fdb866741'

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_2182905134" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2182905134" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2182905134?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781421597713" href="/book/show/34852843-death-note">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59458347-petrik?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2182905134" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5649530487305226861"><b>Death Note is a masterwork that eventually will become a classic in the manga/anime industry, it already did in my opinion.</b><br/><br/>This is my first ever manga review on Goodreads and probably will be my last unless a special edition like this comes out again in the future. I know it’s stated in my profile that I will not review any manga I’ve read because of the sheer amount of volumes manga usually has and the ridiculous amount of manga I’ve read (including reread, it has reached at least 2000 volumes)</span>
  <span id="freeText5649530487305226861" style="display:none"><b>Death Note is a masterwork that eventually will become a classic in the manga/anime industry, it already did in my opinion.</b><br><br>This is my first ever manga review on Goodreads and probably will be my last unless a special edition like this comes out again in the future. I know it’s stated in my profile that I will not review any manga I’ve read because of the sheer amount of volumes manga usually has and the ridiculous amount of manga I’ve read (including reread, it has reached at least 2000 volumes) but I’ll have to make an exception because of this particular <b>Death Note: All-in-One edition.</b> This is not a box set, this is a single 2400 pages paperback that miraculously encompassed all 12 volumes of Death Note and one never before released epilogue chapter in English into one. I’ll get into more detail on this edition at the last section of my review, now let’s get on with the review of the series itself. This review will be completely spoiler-free like always.<br><br>Throughout my time on Goodreads, I’ve been asked several times on which manga I’ll recommend, I have a different type of recommendations depending on who’s asking and what they're looking for but Death Note is one of the few manga that I always recommend to everyone. This is in fact the third time I reread the entire series and including watching the entire anime adaptation two times, this means that this is the fifth time I've experienced the story and it’s still as amazing as ever. I’m really confident to say that this is a manga/anime that will appeal to almost everyone due to how appealing the storyline and artworks are.<br><br>For those of you who don’t know, Death Note is a manga created by the now famous duo Tsugumi Ohba (the writer) and Takeshi Obata (the artist) that has its run from 2003-2006, it is their first collaboration and what made them became one of the most highly acclaimed duos in the industry. Death Note’s genre, in general, can be stated as thriller and mystery with a bit of fantasy going on, but this doesn’t mean that this series will only appeal to the fans of the genres. Unlike novels, manga usually needed a few volumes for the story to get going, if you’re really expecting to be impressed by only one volume, the majority of manga won’t work for you. That said, Death Note is one of the very few manga that managed to grab my attention immediately right from the first chapter for its originality and simplicity concept.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“The name of the human who is written in this note shall die.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>That may sound highly simplistic now that this series has become famous but think about it, who the heck could come with up with this idea in the first place? It seriously never crossed my mind to think someone would actually start a story that revolves around this concept and made it so damn good. Death Note is an incredibly compelling series that focused highly on justice and moral compass. It’s one of the most thought-provoking series I’ve ever read/watched out of all medium and to this day, I still think about what would happen to this world if Death Note truly exists.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Start looking around you... and all you see are people the world would be better off without.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>Let’s be honest, every one of us has at least considered this line of thinking at least once; I still do sometimes, that’s part of being human when everything you hear around the world is injustice. The main character, Light/Kira Yagami is a genius that accidentally obtained a Death Note and uses it for one single purpose: to make the world a better place by killing all scums, rapist, criminals that exist in the world; untouched or touched bylaws, there’s no exception. This makes him an ultimate vigilante that practically can’t be found by anybody because of its killing method, almost as if he was truly a god. The plot, of course, became more complicated once his main rival, L, came into play. Not only Kira and L are both one of the finest characters I’ve ever read out of all medium, their rivalry is also one of the most highly praised rivalry in the world of manga/anime for many great reasons. To state a few, their characterizations and their game of cat and mouse are so well portrayed that you can’t help but root for both of them. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1513009214i/24655948._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Kira Yagami is also one of the reason—the other two being Guts from Berserk and Lelouch from Code Geass—why I have very high standards towards grimdark novel characters. Up until now, I still haven’t come across anyone who can write any grimdark characters as good as these three, not even close.<br><br>The majority of fans think the series got weaker during the second half of the series, I personally disagree. Death Note glued me to the page from the start up until the end that even during my third reread, it still remains very compelling to read. I won’t go into tons of detail why this series is so special, but let me just say that there are magnificent plot and artworks aside, a myriad of moral compass aligned with me. Everyone got their own sense of justice and I won’t bother you with any political/philosophical talk about justice, <b>just read this brilliant masterpiece.</b><br><br>It’s a highly influential immersive series that in fact, it has sparked tons of real-life copycat crimes and attempted malicious behavior around the world, mostly among students. One minor case for example: In May 2010, a middle school student in Avonworth School District in Pennsylvania was suspended for a "Death Note" with names of fellow students and pop singer Justin Bieber. This is of course just one case out of many, you can search up Death Note copycat crimes and you’ll find shitloads of it. This is not a good thing of course, but looking at the bright side, this also shows just how damn good this series is that it managed to influence so many people around the world; whether good or bad, it just depends on the recipient.<br><br>For newcomers to this series, I know Death Note has been adapted several times. But trust me, don’t watch any of the live adaptations, they just pale in comparison, it’s like comparing the smell of perfume to excrement, especially the newly released Netflix adaptation. If you check your desktop, there’s this little icon called “recycle bin”, the Netflix adaptation belongs there, it’s pure garbage. You want the best version of Death Note? Read the manga or watch the anime adaptation.<br><br>Before I close this review, let’s talk a bit about this edition. I strongly encourage you to get this all in one edition. Novels are expensive but they’re nothing compared to manga or graphic novels. Manga are extremely expensive when you think about how fast it is to read one volume, which usually costs $10. Death Note consists of 12 volumes and to get all of them or the box set, you at least have to pay $90-$120 depending on which edition you get. This All-in-One edition is just cheap as fuck, it allows you to get the entire series for $30-$40 depending on where you purchase it from. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1513009214i/24655949._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1513009214i/24655950._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There is no downside to this edition in my opinion other than it is heavy. Look at it this way, how do you read hardcover novels? I usually lay them down on the desk or my bed and read it because reading while lifting hardcovers is the same as asking me to become One Punch Man. This edition can be read like the way you read your hardcover, you don’t have to worry about breaking the spine. The spine is made of enhanced binding technology that made it extremely durable, it’s even stronger than the floppy trade paperback for novels. I read the entire series without any worries due to how durable the book is and I can safely say it’s almost impossible to break the spine unless of course you purposely bend it like Beckham’s feet repeatedly. If you’re still not sure, check out this youtube video and fast forward to 6:00 timestamp to see how extremely durable this edition is.<br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=SGq3XW5ARKU&amp;t=2s">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=SGq3X...</a><br><br><b>In conclusion, Death Note is one of the best manga series I’ve ever read.</b> Give it a few more years and it will become a classic in the genre, in my opinion it already did. It’s one of the most popular manga/anime of all time and one I will always recommend. Once again, dive into this series either through reading the manga or watching the anime, those are the only options you should consider, you can thank me later for one of the best escapism experience once you get to it. Also, I would like to give my special thanks to my dear friend Haifa for getting me this fantastic edition as my early X-mas present.<br><br><i>You can find the rest of my Adult Epic/High Fantasy &amp; Sci-Fi reviews at <b><a href="http://booknest.eu/review/patrick" rel="nofollow noopener">BookNest</a></b></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="5649530487305226861" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2245596223?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TS Chan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TS Chan" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan">TS Chan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781421597713" href="/book/show/34852843-death-note">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=physical-owned">physical-owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2245596223" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10589101068112850354"><b>Brilliant. Ingenious. Masterpiece.</b><br/><br/>So says one who has just been exposed to manga for the very first time through this ever-popular title; one so famous that I've heard of it long before this mammoth 2,400-page all-in-edition was ever released. <br/><br/>As this is my first-ever manga, I can't draw upon experience in this genre to provide a meaningful benchmark. However, manga or novel, one reads for the storytelling and its characters. In both aspects, Death Note excels beyond any shadow of a doubt. Kira,</span>
  <span id="freeText10589101068112850354" style="display:none"><b>Brilliant. Ingenious. Masterpiece.</b><br /><br />So says one who has just been exposed to manga for the very first time through this ever-popular title; one so famous that I've heard of it long before this mammoth 2,400-page all-in-edition was ever released. <br /><br />As this is my first-ever manga, I can't draw upon experience in this genre to provide a meaningful benchmark. However, manga or novel, one reads for the storytelling and its characters. In both aspects, Death Note excels beyond any shadow of a doubt. Kira, the protagonist in Death Note has to be one of the most complex grimdark characters I've encountered and I find myself being torn between cheering him on towards his ultimate goal and being disgusted with his methods to achieve it. <br /><br />There are two major arcs in the entire series, with the first one being slightly longer as well as way more compelling than the final one. I'll just call it the Battle of Two Geniuses - one of the best and most captivating rivalries I've ever read. Although it suffered in comparison, the second arc is still a great cohesive continuation of the story to get us to the climax; slowly building up to a mind-blowing endgame.<br /><br />The art is something else to behold, and this all-in-one edition also compiles the covers of the original published volumes. I often find myself flipping through the book and staring (perhaps even drooling) at the gorgeous artwork. <br /><br />While I am not sure if I will try more mangas in the future, this is one that I will definitely come back to via the very well-acclaimed anime version. The Netflix interpretation just made me cringe and laugh. <br /><br />Last but not least, I will like to end this quick review by thanking my dear friend, Mary, for getting me this incredible thing of beauty for Christmas.</span>

<div id="review_2110843137" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2110843137" />
    <a title="Elizabeth (Elzburg)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26150006-elizabeth-elzburg"><img alt="Elizabeth (Elzburg)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542862303p2/26150006.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2110843137?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth (Elzburg)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth (Elzburg)" href="/user/show/26150006-elizabeth-elzburg">Elizabeth (Elzburg)</a>
      </span>

          marked it as on-hold


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781421597713" href="/book/show/34852843-death-note">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26150006-elizabeth-elzburg?shelf=manga">manga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26150006-elizabeth-elzburg?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2110843137" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15676189341784086356">Death Note is a fantastic 5/5 series, but I want to make some details about this specific edition clear to potential buyers.<br/><br/>THIS IS NOT A BOXSET. It is a single paperback book that has all 2400 pages of the manga, including "a never before printed in English epilogue". It's obviously really thick (and really heavy), but it is also actually quite short (in terms of height; Not page length). It is the shortest book out of my entire manga and graphic novel collection. Even my authentic Japanese imp</span>
  <span id="freeText15676189341784086356" style="display:none">Death Note is a fantastic 5/5 series, but I want to make some details about this specific edition clear to potential buyers.<br /><br />THIS IS NOT A BOXSET. It is a single paperback book that has all 2400 pages of the manga, including "a never before printed in English epilogue". It's obviously really thick (and really heavy), but it is also actually quite short (in terms of height; Not page length). It is the shortest book out of my entire manga and graphic novel collection. Even my authentic Japanese imports (which are always tiny for some reason) are taller than it. The front and back covers are somewhat flimsy, so you'll have to be careful while reading it not to bend/rip it or open it too wide if you don't want to get dents in the spine. And unlike the single volume and Black editions, the first few pages are not printed in their glorious full colour. That, to me, is the biggest blow. Also: In case you have your hopes up about the sides of the pages of this edition also being black, they're not. But the pages are not the average rough paper. This edition is printed on a smooth paper that reminds me of the pages of a magazine, which is something that makes it feel kind of special to flip through. Beware of large black areas though, for they will easily become fingerprint-central if you touch them.<br /><br />All of that is concerning the construction of this edition, but of course the insides (besides the lack of some colour) are the same great Death Note. So if none of those things are huge turn-offs for you then this edition is a great way to be able to read the entire series while saving a lot of money and space on your shelves. I managed to buy this edition for only $25.25 CAD (on sale), which was an enormous steal (compared to buying the whole series individually).<br /><br />While I'm here let's do a whole price comparison on all the different ways you can buy this series: <blockquote><u>Buying all volumes individually:</u> <b>$98.49</b><br /><u>Buying the Black editions:</u> <b>$75.30</b><br /><u>Buying the box set:</u> <b>$74.24</b><br /><u>Buying the omnibus:</u> <b>$32.47</b></blockquote> (All prices listed in CAD and Amazon.ca prices, don't include tax/shipping, and will obviously fluctuate with time.)<br /><br /> I chose to list the Amazon prices and not the list prices because the list prices are always way more expensive so you never buy anything at list price anyway. Like the omnibus list price is technically $53.99, so I could say "Wow I got it for more than 50% off!!!", but we all know that ain't nobody going to actually buy it for that price anyway. Literally every single good bookseller is selling it for less than that.<br /><br />Anyway, if you're okay with spending $75 dollars, I recommend the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6345999.Death_Note_Black_Edition__Vol__1" title="Death Note Black Edition, Vol. 1 by Tsugumi Ohba" rel="nofollow noopener">Black editions</a> as being by far the best way to read this series. They look gorgeous on and off your shelf, and they're nice and big (but not too big) so you can get a real good look at all of the pages.<br /><br /><br /><i>Please consider giving this review a "Like" (it helps me out a lot), and <a href="http://www.bit.ly/elzburg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">follow me</a> if you want more!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="15676189341784086356" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_38960696" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38960696" />
    <a title="Aaron" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1538729-aaron"><img alt="Aaron" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1221691464p2/1538729.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/38960696?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aaron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aaron" href="/user/show/1538729-aaron">Aaron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1538729-aaron?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1538729-aaron?shelf=philosophy-religion">philosophy-religion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1538729-aaron?shelf=sets-the-standard">sets-the-standard</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1538729-aaron?shelf=manga-comic">manga-comic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer38960696" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3759622014884996932">Shakespearean. <i>Death Note</i> the anime stands out as perhaps the single best anime adaptation of manga, which itself is perhaps the best manga of all time. <br/><br/>On the surface <i>Death Note</i> is a fairly straightforward story of cat and mouse, with the best detectives in the world trying to catch the mysterious Kira ("killer"), the alter ego of high school student Light Yagumi. Yagami gains the mysterious death note by accident (dropped in the human world by a <i>shinigami</i> - literally Death God - for amusement)</span>
  <span id="freeText3759622014884996932" style="display:none">Shakespearean. <i>Death Note</i> the anime stands out as perhaps the single best anime adaptation of manga, which itself is perhaps the best manga of all time. <br /><br />On the surface <i>Death Note</i> is a fairly straightforward story of cat and mouse, with the best detectives in the world trying to catch the mysterious Kira ("killer"), the alter ego of high school student Light Yagumi. Yagami gains the mysterious death note by accident (dropped in the human world by a <i>shinigami</i> - literally Death God - for amusement). He quickly decides to use it to rid the world of criminals and to create a new world order, with him as its god. Before long the authorities are after him. He tries to eliminate his pursuers by uncovering their identities without betraying himself as the culprit, and the plot necessarily becomes extremely complex and exciting. Moral dilemmas and suspenseful thrills appear throughout as Kira must constantly decide just how far he will go to protect himself and also to build a world where criminals are killed at the stroke of his pen. <br /><br />I'm a big fan of detective stories, and this is probably my all time favorite. The supernatural element is mostly background to provide new "rules" and give the story several interesting twists. The detail and realism is impressive; characters are very consistent and all the advancements in the plot play out naturally and convincingly (especially considering the supernatural elements involved). The series is 12 volumes (and a "bonus" volume) and it's a real page turner throughout. I was often surprised to find myself so wrapped up in the story on print, especially since I had already seen the anime and new the outcome. <br /><br />The manga goes into greater depth than the anime, expanding on the main storyline and drawing out more details. Also, the audience has more of a window into the thoughts and concerns of the detectives. World class detective "L," for example, expresses more doubt in his own theories, and so seems less superhuman. <br /><br />If you are not normally into manga, I would strongly recommend this series as a good place to start. Recommended for detective story fans, logicians, suspense fans, and anyone into moral dilemmas or ethics. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3759622014884996932" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_145526665" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/145526665" />
    <a title="Steve Giordano" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4155884-steve-giordano"><img alt="Steve Giordano" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/145526665?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steve Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steve Giordano" href="/user/show/4155884-steve-giordano">Steve Giordano</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4155884-steve-giordano?shelf=comic-books">comic-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer145526665" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15445635044188949886">Instead of reviewing all the individual separately, I figured it was easier to write one big review on all the volumes of the series.<br/><br/>What can I say about Death Note, the story of Light Yagami and his quest to change the world "for the better" through the use of the Death Note, a powerful, mystical object that allows him to kill anyone by writing down their name? I can start by saying that it absolutely floored me like no other story has done in a long while.<br/><br/>Death Note, a twelve-volume series wri</span>
  <span id="freeText15445635044188949886" style="display:none">Instead of reviewing all the individual separately, I figured it was easier to write one big review on all the volumes of the series.<br /><br />What can I say about Death Note, the story of Light Yagami and his quest to change the world "for the better" through the use of the Death Note, a powerful, mystical object that allows him to kill anyone by writing down their name? I can start by saying that it absolutely floored me like no other story has done in a long while.<br /><br />Death Note, a twelve-volume series written by Tsugumi Ohba and illustrated by Takeshi Obata, is one of the most complex, well-thought-out, and utterly mindbending stories I have ever read. Truly, Ohba must be of some genius-level intellect to have crafted this tale. The way he displays the thought processes of Light and L, the world-class detective charged with Light's capture, is utterly astounding. The method by which each one of them develops their plans, anticipates the other's plan, and formulates a counterplan... it's mind boggling. And it also makes for a great, great read.<br /><br />Not only is this a story that challenges you intellectually, it also challenges you ethically and philosophically. Light's goal is to change the world by killing off society's bad elements. But in his quest for complete peace, is it okay to kill the good people who seek to stop him? If these people are trying to prevent Utopia, doesn't that make them evil? In wars, casualties are always going to occur. But doesn't the death of a few justify saving the lives of the many? That's one of the many questions that Ohba poses, one that cannot be answered easily.<br /><br />This story will truly get both your thoughts and your heart racing, and I know I'll have a hard time thinking of anything else for the next few days. Or weeks.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15445635044188949886" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13159452303434234682" style="display:none">Brilliant detective story with a really original plot. All the characters, dialogues and deductions are fantastic with perfect illustration. <br />The twists and dynamics are so interesting that you just don't want to put it down - which can be strange after holding 2400 pages for hours :) <br />From Christian perspective Light's character reminds me the exact metaphor of the Devil/accuser/Lucifer(light-bearer). He wants to play God and pass judgement on people by himself. For me the main message of the whole book is <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[“Judge not, lest you be judged” (Matthew 7:1) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I would recommend the book for those who love quality suspense, mystery, detective stories - even if you don't like manga genre. Not recommended for readers who don't like dark, supernatual elements in the plot. </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Felix" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Felix" href="/user/show/22327118-felix">Felix</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22327118-felix?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22327118-felix?shelf=japanese">japanese</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3650951605" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7889606306887325788">This was a lot of fun. I feel like <i>Death Note</i> has been so hyped since it was published that it is hard for it to live up to its reputation, but it was satisfying nonetheless. I was worried that such a long serial would end with a damp squib, but it didn't. It dragged a little around the middle, but it gathered a lot of energy on the run up to its conclusion. Its mysteries were surprisingly intellectually involved. This is easy reading, but the whole mystery side of it doesn't lack complexity. It</span>
  <span id="freeText7889606306887325788" style="display:none">This was a lot of fun. I feel like <i>Death Note</i> has been so hyped since it was published that it is hard for it to live up to its reputation, but it was satisfying nonetheless. I was worried that such a long serial would end with a damp squib, but it didn't. It dragged a little around the middle, but it gathered a lot of energy on the run up to its conclusion. Its mysteries were surprisingly intellectually involved. This is easy reading, but the whole mystery side of it doesn't lack complexity. It's a lot like like <i>Sherlock Holmes</i>, but more complicated, longer, more Japanese, more supernatural, set in a different cultural context, set in a different period, written for a different audience, told through a totally different medium of story-telling, and uhhh... actually perhaps it isn't so much like <i>Sherlock Holmes</i> as I thought it was. It's still fun though.</span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1269483998" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1269483998" />
    <a title="Michaela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7346032-michaela"><img alt="Michaela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1346274846p2/7346032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1269483998?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michaela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michaela" href="/user/show/7346032-michaela">Michaela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1269483998" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2308675598256030242">Note: No major spoilers<br/><br/>Death Note is an intelligent and meticulously illustrated rollercoaster ride. With hardly a dull moment, it will keep you turning pages hours after you thought you would be doing something else. The artwork is superb, and while the author of the story, Ohba Tsugumi, is sometimes thought to be a bit too wordy, the story is complex enough to need all those words, even if you are in a bit of a hurry to turn the next page and find out what will happen. Suspenseful is the best </span>
  <span id="freeText2308675598256030242" style="display:none">Note: No major spoilers<br /><br />Death Note is an intelligent and meticulously illustrated rollercoaster ride. With hardly a dull moment, it will keep you turning pages hours after you thought you would be doing something else. The artwork is superb, and while the author of the story, Ohba Tsugumi, is sometimes thought to be a bit too wordy, the story is complex enough to need all those words, even if you are in a bit of a hurry to turn the next page and find out what will happen. Suspenseful is the best word to describe this series, although it is actually not very action-packed. There is much thinking and strategizing, as well as wonderful sparring matches between the main characters. The characters themselves drive the story forward as well, and they are almost all formidable in some way.<br /><br />Light Yagami, our antihero, is a high school student who has stumbled upon the power to kill in the form of a black notebook, which contains the words: “The human whose name is written in this note shall die.” He asserts that “There's something about the Death Note itself that makes humans want to try it out at least once,” but he does far more than that. With his newfound power he sets about to “Eliminate the vermin from the world,” even at the cost of his own mind and soul.<br /><br />I despised Light Yagami in almost every way. I pity him only marginally because of his circumstances (had he not found the death note, I am pretty sure he would have lead a fairly normal life, though that's not to say he wasn't responsible for his actions when he found it), and although I held my breath many a time, waiting for and even almost subconsciously hoping for his escapes from various traps set for him, I was always hoping for his eventual capture and confinement, if not his demise. Arrogant, without a care for the lives of those who stand in his way, he only gets worse as he gets older. The second half of the series, which takes place a few years after the first, presents an even colder and more despicable characterization as with the misplaced power of a god, he seems less and less like a human being and more and more like something utterly inferior.<br /><br />A mastermind known only as L is Light Yagami’s chief opponent. Quirky and highly unusual, his every move in both the investigation and in each scene is hugely entertaining and comical. His adamant declaration that “The good guys always win,” combined with his persistent investigation when he has a hunch and his keen eye for behavioral inconsistencies make him the perfect answer to Light’s intelligent scheming and dubious assessments of right and wrong. He is like some kind of funky Sherlock Holmes, and the way he respectfully attaches san or kun to everyone’s name puts me in mind of Lieutenant Columbo, who without fail addressed everyone (and most notably his suspects) as sir or ma’am.<br /><br />Enter Near and Mello, two other odd individuals who are just as determined as L to apprehend the vigilante serial killer known as Kira.<br /><br />Mello is somewhat less of a threat to Light as he too often allows his emotions to control him, and I mostly disliked him. He’s a bit creepy and definitely more ambiguous than L; his motive is not justice but the desire to defeat his rival, Near, and he even does some things that are as bad as what Light himself does. But I liked him a little better later on, and I think he was the human element that the series needed at that halfway point. While brilliant and idiosyncratic, he wasn’t so unbelievable as L or Near.<br /><br />Near is much like L. Objective and queer, he quickly becomes more of a pain in Light’s side than the impassioned Mello and it is pretty mind-blowing to watch his investigation. <br /><br />By the time you’ve read 12 volumes of this supernatural thriller, you almost believe that the battle between Light and his opponents will never end, and so it’s also a bit strange when it does. But the ending is pretty satisfying. <br /><br />All in all, this series is close to perfect. 9/10</span>
  <a data-text-id="2308675598256030242" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_134068475" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/134068475" />
    <a title="Chris Merritt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2427935-chris-merritt"><img alt="Chris Merritt" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/134068475?book_show_action=true">Dec 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris Merritt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris Merritt" href="/user/show/2427935-chris-merritt">Chris Merritt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer134068475" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13184049949694684451">Not everyone is a fan of manga. Some people can't get past the idea of comics being used to tell a serious story, other people just don't like the style of art in manga with over-exagerrated expressions, large eyes, etc. However, the unique nature of this one should be worth looking into. In the Shinigami (Death God) realm, the Shinigami have forgotten their purpose and spend their time gambling away years of their lives. However, each has a Death Note, and by writing the name of a human into it</span>
  <span id="freeText13184049949694684451" style="display:none">Not everyone is a fan of manga. Some people can't get past the idea of comics being used to tell a serious story, other people just don't like the style of art in manga with over-exagerrated expressions, large eyes, etc. However, the unique nature of this one should be worth looking into. In the Shinigami (Death God) realm, the Shinigami have forgotten their purpose and spend their time gambling away years of their lives. However, each has a Death Note, and by writing the name of a human into it, they kill the human and steal the remainder of their life for themselves.<br /><br />Ryuk has grown bored with this existance and in an effort to find some entertainment, he drops a Death Note filled with the rules for its use on Earth, where similarly bored Light Yagami, a brilliant student, finds it. Thinking it is a joke, he tries using it, and ends up killing a criminal who had taken hostages. Realizing the power of what he has found, he proceeds to create a new world for good people where there are no criminals.<br /><br />As more and more criminals die, the police of the world gather to discuss the case. At Interpol, the mysterious detective, known only as L, expresses interest in the case and vows to catch the killer. Thus begins an incredible battle of wits and wills between two brilliant minds both intent on defeating the other.<br /><br />Occasionally the story goes a bit over the top or edges into the ridiculous, and in the middle of the series there is a quick four year advance in time that is a bit jarring and takes the story in a new direction, but overall the story, writing, and artwork are spot on in bringing a world where Shinigami can exist to life. Is Light a savior to the world, or nothing more than a mass murderer? Can he stay ahead of L or will he end up as just another closed case for the detective? I highly recommend this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13184049949694684451" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_739987068" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/739987068" />
    <a title="Natalie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17215023-natalie"><img alt="Natalie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593997066p2/17215023.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/739987068?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie" href="/user/show/17215023-natalie">Natalie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Natalie by: </span>
      Shounen Jump 
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17215023-natalie?shelf=manga">manga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17215023-natalie?shelf=shounen-manga">shounen-manga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17215023-natalie?shelf=brilliant">brilliant</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17215023-natalie?shelf=really-good-characters">really-good-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17215023-natalie?shelf=clever">clever</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17215023-natalie?shelf=colorful-characters">colorful-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17215023-natalie?shelf=rereading">rereading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17215023-natalie?shelf=fun">fun</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17215023-natalie?shelf=shinigami">shinigami</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17215023-natalie?shelf=action">action</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer739987068" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9781492825621602694">I absolutely LOVE Death Note. The way the story flows and the character development is phenomenal. Why is it good? Because everything in this series is done <i>perfectly.</i> The main characters are perfect. The story is perfect. The character designs are perfect. The tension and drama is perfect. Even the side characters are perfect. This manga is just too awesome and wonderful to love.<br/><br/>The story is basically a cat and mouse chase between the criminal killer Kira, and the best detective in the world L.</span>
  <span id="freeText9781492825621602694" style="display:none">I absolutely LOVE Death Note. The way the story flows and the character development is phenomenal. Why is it good? Because everything in this series is done <i>perfectly.</i> The main characters are perfect. The story is perfect. The character designs are perfect. The tension and drama is perfect. Even the side characters are perfect. This manga is just too awesome and wonderful to love.<br /><br />The story is basically a cat and mouse chase between the criminal killer Kira, and the best detective in the world L. Both are trying to stop the other and bring the other to justice. <br /><br />I really like the suspense that this manga gives the readers. I also like how the author gives both the protagonist and the antagonist different personalities that make them unique and NOT perfect. They each have their own flaws and certain characteristics that make them likable characters and assist the readers (well some readers anyway) with struggling in choosing which side to support. This manga goes back and forth with Kira and L and it succeeds in changing the sides of the audience by mere decisions that the characters make that make the audience either love or hate them.<br /><br />What is really interesting is how the protagonist is portrayed as the villain and the antagonist is portrayed as the hero. But the way its portrayed is not settled, because L is a detective that is supposed to work for the 'good guys' because he is searching for a criminal and Kira is supposedly the 'bad guy' because there are arguments on how he has no right to kill criminals because he has no authority to judge and act based on his judgment. There is also the other side of these arguments that say 'Why <i>shouldn't</i> he kill these criminals? They deserve it right?' This constant switching back and forth between which character you're going to choose sides with is what keeps readers invested and interested into reading and thinking about what's going to happen to these characters.<br /><br />Light Yagami (aka Kira) is a college student (he was a high school student at the beginning of the series) who was bored with his life until a bored Shinigami named Ryuk who dropped his notebook in the human world so a human could pick it up. What amazes me about this character is that he is <b>not</b> just a typical teenager that the author chose as his protagonist. Light is just <b>great</b> character. He's smart, he studies, he's confident, logical, deceptive, clever, resourceful, and <i>bored.</i> He's bored with his life that when he picks up the Death Note and uses it because he's frustrated with the justice of the world. Personally, I just LOVE this character. He's is just so complex and so likable even though he sometimes makes decisions that question his judgement. It also made the character unpredictable about how could he avoid the police and it allowed the direction of the series to be unpredictable. And I love books that can do that. He also has a partner (in a sense) a shinigami named Ryuk.<br /><br />First of all I LOVE Ryuk. He is an awesome character with a unique personality and is a lot of fun to read/watch (depending on if you read the manga or watched the anime). He has interesting traits that make him a unique character. For example, his addiction to apples. His withdrawal symptoms of not eating apples are <s>pretty funny</s> really hilarious and his shyness around girls is really interesting considering that he is a Shinigami. I also love him not interfering with Light and his role as Kira. I find it very interesting to see how Ryuk watches Light's actions and doesn't interfere unless it is a bother or a benefit to Ryuk. One example is when Ryuk tells Light there is somebody following him only because it was getting on Ryuk's nerves.<br /><br />There is also Misa Amane. I'm not really sure what to think of her honestly. She has a personality that is likable at times and her design is just great. Granted, she got annoying at times but all she wanted was to help Light in any way she can because he killed the killer that killed her parents and so she's grateful to him. He didn't even love her. Correct me if I'm wrong, but <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[didn't she kill herself after Light's death in the end? I don't know if it was the manga or the anime, but she jumped off a building after Light had died. Right? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> She was just being used by Light. Poor girl.<br /><br />Then there is Rem and some of the police involved with the Kira case they're also a lot of fun and have their own personalities. The two cops that stand out to me were Soichiro Yagami, Light's father, and Touta Matsuda. Soichiro is trying to handle being a father but also trying to bring Kira to justice at the same time. When his son is taken to prison after being suspected to be Kira, he becomes depressed and asks to be placed in prison as well because he feels that he will lose control. You really feel for this guy. His son is accused of being a dangerous criminal and he's trying to stop him. You can feel the pain he's going through and it's understandable when we see the emotions that he portrays. Matsuda is also pretty likable as well. I personally think this character is AWESOME!!!!!!!<br /><br />-_-' . . . . . . . . <br /><br />Ok, I'm sorry. But I'm a sucker for characters like Matsuda. He's inexperienced but he's dedicated. He's clumsy and makes mistakes but he has a good heart. He's naive and speaks his mind but he is also trying to help the task force as much as he could. Now let me make it clear when I say that <b>this character is not new, we've seen this idiot before.</b> He naive but he's got a good heart. He's clumsy but determined. I guess why he's so likable is because he seems like he has a personality that I've never seen before even though I've seen this character many times. I think the reason why it works so much is because he's not the main character but a side character instead. Such a dork, but I still enjoy him.<br /><br />Another character I LOVE is L, or Ryuzaki. L is just awesome. I love how he is the enemy of Light but also the opposite of Light. Light seems like an everyday smart person you could get along with and enjoy being around. He dresses professionally and he is good at what he does. L's design is the opposite. His appearance is an unusual appearance that gives him a look that would keep people away from him if they didn't know who was. (I'm sorry but its true) He sits in an awkward position, dresses strangely, has bags under his eyes, and eats a lot of sweets. L is just so <b>awesome</b> that I just enjoy him so much. If I did have one complaint, it would be that he died. *sniffs &amp; sobs* L, WE WILL MISS YOU! I know that some people hate the arc after L's death but I still find it enjoyable even though L is no longer there. Near is ok, he’s not as great as L but I still love it to the end.<br /><br />I really love the beginning of the plot. Kira is created from an intelligent, bored young man and a bored Shinigami who come together with a death note as the key with Light's goal of becoming the "God of the New World." His motivation is really interesting on how it just started on mere <i>boredom.</i> I guess that's what makes Light so complex and so interesting. His design is so great that you really get invested. <br /><br />As far as I'm aware, I know that there is debate on whether Light's actions were good or evil but it really doesn't make a whole lot of difference to me because both arguments work and seem reasonable because this series is so good that is allows audiences to debate on which side to take. I really like the change (or progression) with Light's character. For better or for worse, Light's character changes and it is because of the death note that he changed. This just makes him an <b>awesome</b> character.<br /><br />Death Note is just flipping awesome and a great reading experience to look forward to. The characters? Memorable. The story? Fantastic. The message(s)? Something good to think about. Even the art in both the manga and anime. The dark colors and setting are just great and sets the tone just right. In closing, Death Note is a great series with great characters portraying great messages. I would say check it out but let’s face it, most of you already have.<br /><br />I will later reread this series and rate the manga volumes individually. Anyways . . . totally LOVE this series!!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9781492825621602694" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781421597713" href="/book/show/34852843-death-note">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2354310970&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2354310970" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5611986897690873894">Death Note is my favorite anime, and I think I enjoyed the manga even more. Most of the conflict revolves around serial killer Light Yagami and his nemesis L, the world’s greatest detective. The characters’ philosophies develop throughout the story, especially after L’s heirs are introduced, and I like how we never get a definite answer on central themes such as justice and righteousness. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('aA+05qD06vguMEGEflRnp143m1Hw38ZW+j9sT6Y0eu1GUsXgQrBu2OCHOX9NolnHODFMgUMeDuP6eMQaZ6MUJg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8HMj1tSFCU13DFBqO4asSUhEvxnfDBckLKjjud2QgdneLlLQNsGNbbm7KJEIcJIpLkJoyWzN35Es70vsHAfvEg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4371472286699350794">Tsugumi Ōba (Profile in Japanese: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19876928.______' title='大場 つぐみ' rel='nofollow noopener'>大場 つぐみ</a>), born in Tokyo, Japan, is a writer best known for the manga Death Note. His/her real identity is a closely guarded secret. As stated by the profile placed at the beginning of each Death Note manga, Ōba collects teacups and develops manga plots while holding his knees on a chair, similar to a habit of L, one of the main characters of the series.<br/><br/>There is spe</span>
  <span id="freeText4371472286699350794" style="display:none">Tsugumi Ōba (Profile in Japanese: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19876928.______" title="大場 つぐみ" rel="nofollow noopener">大場 つぐみ</a>), born in Tokyo, Japan, is a writer best known for the manga Death Note. His/her real identity is a closely guarded secret. As stated by the profile placed at the beginning of each Death Note manga, Ōba collects teacups and develops manga plots while holding his knees on a chair, similar to a habit of L, one of the main characters of the series.<br /><br />There is speculation that Tsugumi Ōba is a pen name and that he is really Hiroshi Gamō. Pointing out that in Bakuman the main character's uncle was a one-hit wonder manga artist who worked on a gag super hero manga, very similar to Gamō and Tottemo! Luckyman in all aspects. Also that the storyboards drawn by Ōba greatly resemble Tottemo! Luckyman in style.</span>
